<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6858ecc4-6c4b-4432-818f-dececeb67a0e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText9830721663060994915" style="display:none">3.5 - 4 stars! <br>Not as exciting as the first two short stories, but definitely worth reading. <br><br><i> "I will not be a pawn, not for them ... and not for my father; I will not belong to anyone but myself." </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509745434ra/24355308.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Son follows Four as he struggles to find his place in the hierarchy of Dauntless. <span id="freeTextContainer15777089280393502454"><u><b>3</b> What I hate, What I love, What I fear <b>★'s</b></u> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Our city is changing...Sometime soon, everyone will have to choose a side”</i>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566085340i/28008614._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“That’s what I really want—to shed all the people who want to form and shape me, one by one, and learn instead to form and shape myself.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566085340i/28008615._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>“You can be more than either, more than any faction.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>The Son</i> was not nearly as good as the first two. It's my least favorite thus far. It was really slow, unexciting, and to be honest, it was very boring. But... it wasn't horrible e</span>
  <span id="freeText15777089280393502454" style="display:none"><u><b>3</b> What I hate, What I love, What I fear <b>★'s</b></u> <br><br><b>
  <i>“Our city is changing...Sometime soon, everyone will have to choose a side”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566085340i/28008614._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“That’s what I really want—to shed all the people who want to form and shape me, one by one, and learn instead to form and shape myself.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566085340i/28008615._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“You can be more than either, more than any faction.”</i>
</b><br><br><i>The Son</i> was not nearly as good as the first two. It's my least favorite thus far. It was really slow, unexciting, and to be honest, it was very boring. But... it wasn't horrible either. This takes place right after he becomes a Dauntless member and gets his apartment and chooses his career path. This novella includes the moment that Four finds out that his mother <i>Evelyn</i> is still alive. But most importantly it shows that Four found out that Max, Eric, and Jeanine were planning something BIG against Abnegation (which all goes down at the end of Divergent) two years prior. And he does absolutely NOTHING to prevent it. Wow, that's some heroicness right there 😠. This just didn't seem very Four like to me. Oh, and he also acknowledges the fact that Dauntless won't be his home forever. I really really didn't like that it changed my opinion of Four even in the slightest and changed the facts I thought I knew in Divergent and Insurgent.<br><br>Moving onto, #0.4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18080923.The_Traitor__Divergent___0_4_" title="The Traitor (Divergent, #0.4) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traitor</a></span>

    <a title="Miriam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10072078-miriam"><img alt="Miriam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383915365p2/10072078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          marked it as not-out-yet

<span id="freeTextContainer2572879215781973742"><i>Squeeeee!!!!</i> I'm learning more about Four!! This is going to be great!!<br/><br/>I really hope it's not about Four's time with Marcus (<i>that bastard!</i>). I can't stand Four being in pain or being unhappy. It will be emotionally painful for me.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>My Four</u>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380433361i/872024.jpg' width='170' height='265' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>P.S This short story is part of <i>Four: A Divergent Story Collection</i> and is the fourth one.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1220243789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8257669479993016739"><b>
  <blockquote>«“This afternoon you’ll pick your job,” Max says. “Did you have anything in mind?”<br/>“I guess that depends on what’s available,” I say. “I’d like to do something with teaching. Like what Amar did, maybe.”»</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>We follow the aftermath of Amar’s “death” with Four choosing what he’d like to do for a living. At the same time, we begin to see Erudite’s infiltration on Dauntless headquarters and their formatting of the leaders to their liking.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>«On the day you hated most<br/>At the time when she died<br/>In the pl</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText8257669479993016739" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>«“This afternoon you’ll pick your job,” Max says. “Did you have anything in mind?”<br />“I guess that depends on what’s available,” I say. “I’d like to do something with teaching. Like what Amar did, maybe.”»</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />We follow the aftermath of Amar’s “death” with Four choosing what he’d like to do for a living. At the same time, we begin to see Erudite’s infiltration on Dauntless headquarters and their formatting of the leaders to their liking.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>«On the day you hated most<br />At the time when she died<br />In the place where you first jumped on.»</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />He thinks it’s Marcus who is contacting him, and it’s heart-breaking to read when he finally understands it was not, and not only did his father not care at all for him, but he lied to him about Evelyn’s death. He’s been betrayed by both of his parents.<br /><br /><blockquote>«“Is even a part of you happy to see me again?”<br />“Happy to see you again?” I say. “I barely remember you, Evelyn. I’ve almost lived as long without you as I did with you.”»</blockquote><br /><br />It’s also very interesting that along with Tori, Evelyn was the trigger for Four’s tattoo and his new perspective on the world.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>«You can be more than either, more than any faction.»</b>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_1922575308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922575308" />
    <a title="Julianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/883725-julianna"><img alt="Julianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442976820p2/883725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922575308?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna" href="/user/show/883725-julianna">Julianna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the Divergent Series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=desert-island-keepers">desert-island-keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922575308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13197471863924742138">Reviewed for <a href='http://www.thcreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>THC Reviews</a><br/>In <i>The Son</i>, the third novella that explores Four’s life before meeting Tris in <i>Divergent</i>, he has completed the Dauntless initiation at the top of his class. As such, he’s eligible to choose pretty much any job he wants within the faction. He thinks he might want to be a trainer, but Max, one of the faction leaders, thinks he’s qualified for much more and wants him to go through the process of trying to become a Dauntless leader. This leads to a lot of contemplations on Fo</span>
  <span id="freeText13197471863924742138" style="display:none">Reviewed for <a href="http://www.thcreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">THC Reviews</a><br />In <i>The Son</i>, the third novella that explores Four’s life before meeting Tris in <i>Divergent</i>, he has completed the Dauntless initiation at the top of his class. As such, he’s eligible to choose pretty much any job he wants within the faction. He thinks he might want to be a trainer, but Max, one of the faction leaders, thinks he’s qualified for much more and wants him to go through the process of trying to become a Dauntless leader. This leads to a lot of contemplations on Four’s part as he tries to decide if this is what he wants to do with his life, while also continuing his rivalry with Eric for the same position. At the same time, Four accidentally discovers that there may be something foul afoot between Dauntless and Erudite, which makes him realize that hiding his “differences” are all the more important. Also for the first time, he hears the term Divergent applied to his awareness during simulations, and he also deals with a shocking revelation from his past. <br /><br />The more of these novellas I read about Four, the more I’m convinced the <i>Divergent</i> series as a whole would have been better, IMHO, if either he had narrated it or if it had been done in dual narration. I’ve been enjoying these stories more than the main part of the series, and one of the reasons why is because they’re written in Four’s perspective. I feel like his character is really developing and coming alive in my mind’s eye far better than he ever did before. And for some reason, this particular story seemed to have an even deeper POV than the previous two or the series in general. Four is still the loner, preferring to take up residence in his own apartment after initiation, rather than with others within the faction, but he does still have a few friends. He also struggles between his two identities as someone who supposedly tested with an aptitude for Abnegation, but fearing his father’s abuse, chose to leave and become Dauntless. Four really starts figuring things out, both in his own life and in the events that are going on around him, which leads to more introspection. Overall, it was a really good read that I very much enjoyed. In addition to feeling more engaged in Four’s POV, I liked seeing more of the secondary characters who become a part of the main series: Eric, Zeke, Uriah, Shauna, Lynn, and Marlene. I also liked learning about the history of various plot points within the <i>Divergent</i> series and how those things came about. It was enlightening as well as entertaining, and very much makes me look forward to reading the final novella in this group of stories about Four.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13197471863924742138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1016451613?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1016451613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13780249081263412704">In this "short" story we see Four adapting to life in Dauntless and how he started to notice the inner working of the leaders there.<br/>We finally, totally understand the exact reason he gave up leadership and how he was almost elected. And it's great to see how smart he is in quickly figuring things out.<br/>What confused me were the small inconsistencies I noticed, or think I did.<br/>Correct me if I'm wrong, but if I'm not mistaken, I'm pretty sure Four was semi-surprised to find out his mother was alive. </span>
  <span id="freeText13780249081263412704" style="display:none">In this "short" story we see Four adapting to life in Dauntless and how he started to notice the inner working of the leaders there.<br />We finally, totally understand the exact reason he gave up leadership and how he was almost elected. And it's great to see how smart he is in quickly figuring things out.<br />What confused me were the small inconsistencies I noticed, or think I did.<br />Correct me if I'm wrong, but if I'm not mistaken, I'm pretty sure Four was semi-surprised to find out his mother was alive. And he was still a little resentful, though later he was a bit of a mama's boy.<br />This story tells us he knew about her being alive way before the events in Divergent and Insurgent. <br />That makes no sense. And towards the end of the story it makes it seem as if he was thinking about joining her later, which would explain why he was so easy later, but then why would he put up resistance if he was already planning on joining her in the future?<br />idk those things confused me about how things took place, but the story in and of itself was pretty good, intriging, and still makes me like Four, so four stars it gets :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13780249081263412704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XEQaPZkYZ7H0vhc2YpqxqJHM/wGX90kqflrGlEBz5ABLU7XLAtykTF+waZzB1W0BMfjZXHl9NrJ+fMw14QKgag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('04XV0tJ6NHNiHwrVJ1VviVnptSXISoME/eWZzLDAGxnEknokSb73jskRdH+EGrMg+d2TeCbA/Jz9w5NtEbFfcw==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_13335037'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037-divergent?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Divergent (Divergent, #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/4039811.Veronica_Roth?origin=series_works\">Veronica Roth<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.19 avg rating &mdash; 2,927,183 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2011\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer13076150578267303659\">In Beatrice Prior\'s dystopian Chicago world, society is divided into five factions, each dedicated to the cultivation of a particular virtue—Candor (the honest), Abnegation (the selfless), Dauntless (the brave), Amity (the peaceful), and Erudite (the<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13076150578267303659\" style=\"display:none\">In Beatrice Prior\'s dystopian Chicago world, society is divided into five factions, each dedicated to the cultivation of a particular virtue—Candor (the honest), Abnegation (the selfless), Dauntless (the brave), Amity (the peaceful), and Erudite (the intelligent). On an appointed day of every year, all sixteen-year-olds must select the faction to which they will devote the rest of their lives. For Beatrice, the decision is between staying with her family and being who she really is—she can\'t have both. So she makes a choice that surprises everyone, including herself.During the highly competitive initiation that follows, Beatrice renames herself Tris and struggles alongside her fellow initiates to live out the choice they have made. Together they must undergo extreme physical tests of endurance and intense psychological simulations, some with devastating consequences.
